<div style="text-align: left; direction: ltr; font-size:70%; color:grey"><a class="mw-kartographer-maplink" data-lat="52.626" data-lon="-1.134" data-overlays='["_89ee5d73b0303d7befa591487252537ec31c5e02"]' data-style="osm-intl" data-zoom="13" href="/wiki/Special:Map/13/52.626/-1.134" mw-data="interface">[Full screen]</a></div>

<p><br/>
<b>Leicester Tigers</b> (officially <b>Leicester Football Club</b>) is an English <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a> club based in <a href="/wiki/Leicester" title="Leicester">Leicester</a>, <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a> that plays in the <a href="/wiki/English_Premiership_(rugby_union)" title="English Premiership (rugby union)">English Premiership</a>.</p>
<p>Leicester are the most successful English club since the introduction of league rugby in 1987, a record 10 times English champions – 4 more than either <a href="/wiki/Bath_Rugby" title="Bath Rugby">Bath</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/London_Wasps" title="London Wasps">Wasps</a>, and last won the <a href="/wiki/English_Premiership_(rugby_union)" title="English Premiership (rugby union)">Premiership</a> title in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2012-13_English_Premiership_(rugby_union)" title="2012-13 English Premiership (rugby union)">2012–13 season</a>. Leicester have also appeared in a record nine successive Premiership finals, from 2005 to 2013. The Tigers have never finished a league season below 6th position, and are one of only four teams (along with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gloucester_RFC" title="Gloucester RFC">Gloucester</a>, Bath and Wasps) never to have been relegated from the top division. Leicester are also the only English side to have qualified to play in every <a href="/wiki/European_Rugby_Champions_Cup" title="European Rugby Champions Cup">European Rugby Champions Cup</a> (and the Heineken Cup which it replaced) in which English teams have participated, and are also the most successful English side in Europe; back-to-back champions in <a href="/wiki/2001_Heineken_Cup_Final" title="2001 Heineken Cup Final">2001</a> and <a href="/wiki/2002_Heineken_Cup_Final" title="2002 Heineken Cup Final">2002</a> and losing finalists in <a href="/wiki/1997_Heineken_Cup_Final" title="1997 Heineken Cup Final">1997</a>, <a href="/wiki/2007_Heineken_Cup_Final" title="2007 Heineken Cup Final">2007</a> and <a href="/wiki/2009_Heineken_Cup_Final" title="2009 Heineken Cup Final">2009</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honours">Honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leicester_Tigers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/English_Premiership_(rugby_union)" title="English Premiership (rugby union)">English Premiership</a> (10)</b>: <a href="/wiki/1987%E2%80%9388_Courage_League" title="1987–88 Courage League">1988</a>, <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_English_Premiership_(rugby_union)" title="1994–95 English Premiership (rugby union)">1995</a>, <a href="/wiki/1998%E2%80%9399_English_Premiership_(rugby_union)" title="1998–99 English Premiership (rugby union)">1999</a>, <a href="/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_English_Premiership_(rugby_union)" title="1999–2000 English Premiership (rugby union)">2000</a>, <a href="/wiki/2000%E2%80%9301_English_Premiership_(rugby_union)" title="2000–01 English Premiership (rugby union)">2001</a>, <a href="/wiki/2001%E2%80%9302_English_Premiership_(rugby_union)" title="2001–02 English Premiership (rugby union)">2002</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_Guinness_Premiership" title="2006–07 Guinness Premiership">2007</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_Guinness_Premiership" title="2008–09 Guinness Premiership">2009</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Guinness_Premiership" title="2009–10 Guinness Premiership">2010</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Aviva_Premiership" title="2012–13 Aviva Premiership">2013</a></li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Minor_Honours">Minor Honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leicester_Tigers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Minor Honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Middlesex_7s" title="Middlesex 7s">Middlesex 7s</a> (1)</b>: 1995</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Aviva_A_League" title="Aviva A League">Aviva A League</a> (4)</b>: 2004–05, 2005–06, 2009–10, 2010–11</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leicester_Tigers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foundation">Foundation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leicester_Tigers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Foundation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:E.Redman_1895.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="835" data-file-width="608" height="247" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/E.Redman_1895.jpg/180px-E.Redman_1895.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/E.Redman_1895.jpg/270px-E.Redman_1895.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/E.Redman_1895.jpg/360px-E.Redman_1895.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:E.Redman_1895.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
E. Redman, Leicester captain in 1895.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Leicester Football Club was formed in a meeting held in the city's George Hotel on 3 August 1880 by the merger of three smaller teams: Leicester Societies AFC, Leicester Amateur FC and Leicester Alert.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> The club's first game was a scoreless draw on 23 October against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moseley_Rugby_Football_Club" title="Moseley Rugby Football Club">Moseley</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Belgrave_Road_Cycle_and_Cricket_Ground" title="Belgrave Road Cycle and Cricket Ground">Belgrave Road Cycle and Cricket Ground</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> That first season Tigers play a local fixture list against the likes of <a href="/wiki/Northampton_Saints" title="Northampton Saints">Northampton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nuneaton_R.F.C." title="Nuneaton R.F.C.">Nuneaton</a>, Rushden, <a href="/wiki/Kettering_Rugby_Football_Club" title="Kettering Rugby Football Club">Kettering</a>, Market Harborough and <a href="/wiki/Coventry_R.F.C." title="Coventry R.F.C.">Coventry</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> In 1881 the club joined the Midlands Counties Football Association enabling them to enter the Midlands Counties Cup the next season. Tigers first ever cup game was an away loss to Edgbaston Crusaders.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_Years">Early Years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leicester_Tigers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Early Years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>This inauspicious start to the cup continued with losses to Moseley in each of the next three seasons. In 1888 Tigers fixture list started to expand outside the midlands, on 10 March they traveled to <a href="/wiki/Valley_Parade" title="Valley Parade">Valley Parade</a> in Bradford to play <a href="/wiki/Manningham_F.C." title="Manningham F.C.">Manningham F.C.</a>, the forerunners of soccer side <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bradford_City" title="Bradford City">Bradford City</a>. The 1888-89 season saw Tigers welcome back Manningham as well as <a href="/wiki/Oldham_Roughyeds" title="Oldham Roughyeds">Oldham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Swinton_Lions" title="Swinton Lions">Swinton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_Harlequins_RFC" title="Cardiff Harlequins RFC">Cardiff Harlequins</a> became the club's first <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Welsh</a> opponents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> Leicester also reached their first Midland Counties Cup Final that year losing, again, to Moseley in front of 4,000 fans in Coventry.</p>
<p>1889-90 saw Tigers travel to <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a> for the first time playing <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_RFC" title="Cardiff RFC">Cardiff</a> and <a href="/wiki/Newport_RFC" title="Newport RFC">Newport</a> on consecutive days, the Monday and Tuesday of Easter week. <a href="/wiki/Gloucester_Rugby" title="Gloucester Rugby">Gloucester</a> were added to the fixture list in 1891-92, whilst on 13 February Tigers played in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> for the first time, a 37-0 loss to <a href="/wiki/Blackheath_F.C." title="Blackheath F.C.">Blackheath</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 10 September 1892 Leicester played their first game at their present ground, <a href="/wiki/Welford_Road_Stadium" title="Welford Road Stadium">Welford Road</a>, against a Leicestershire XV. That season saw derby matches produce attendances up to 7,000 whilst 10,000 saw Leicester lose 12-0 to <a href="/wiki/Coventry_R.F.C." title="Coventry R.F.C.">Coventry</a> in the second round of the Midlands Counties Cup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tom_Crumbie_and_the_rise_to_national_prominence">Tom Crumbie and the rise to national prominence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leicester_Tigers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Tom Crumbie and the rise to national prominence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Tom_Crumbie" title="Tom Crumbie">Tom Crumbie</a> was appointed secretary on 2 August 1895, a position he held for the next 33 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> Crumbie has been credited with dragging the club to national prominence, he disbanded reserve and third teams making the First XV an invitation side and introducing players from all over the country. During his tenure 26 players from the club became capped at international level.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Midlands Counties Cup was secured for the first time in 1898; captain <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Jones_(cricketer)" title="Arthur Jones (cricketer)">Arthur Jones</a> lead the club to victories over <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Lions" title="Rugby Lions">Rugby</a> (31-0), <a href="/wiki/Burton_RFC" title="Burton RFC">Burton</a> (17-0) and <a href="/wiki/Coventry_R.F.C." title="Coventry R.F.C.">Coventry</a> (12-5) to reach the final against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moseley_Rugby_Football_Club" title="Moseley Rugby Football Club">Moseley</a> played on Wednesday 6 April at Coventry's Butts ground. Jones was forced to miss the final on medical grounds but Tigers still took home the cup for the first time winning 5-3. The only score coming from Percy Oscroft after only 3 minutes, the try converted by Frank Jones, Arthur's brother.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>Leicester's first defense of the cup was against local club Belgrave St Peter's, dispatched 68-3, and Tigers progressed to the final again in 1899 first requiring a replay to beat old rivals Moseley in the semi finals. In the final <a href="/wiki/Nuneaton_R.F.C." title="Nuneaton R.F.C.">Nuneaton</a> were beaten 20-3. For the next three seasons Leicester had the better of Moseley beating them in the final each year, before seeing off Rugby in the final of 1903. Moseley were defeated again in 1904, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nottingham_Rugby" title="Nottingham Rugby">Nottingham</a> beaten 31-0 in 1905. Having won the Midlands Counties Cup every year from 1898 to 1905, they dropped out "to give other teams a chance".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1903 <a href="/wiki/Jack_Miles_(rugby_union)" title="Jack Miles (rugby union)">Jack Miles</a> became the first home produced <a href="/wiki/England_national_rugby_union_team" title="England national rugby union team">England</a> international, playing on the wing against <a href="/wiki/Wales_national_rugby_union_team" title="Wales national rugby union team">Wales</a> in <a href="/wiki/Swansea" title="Swansea">Swansea</a>. He had come to prominence scoring 43 tries in 52 appearances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>Leicester's status as a premier club was confirmed in 1905 when a crowd of 20,000 was on hand to see the club face <a href="/wiki/The_Original_All_Blacks" title="The Original All Blacks">The Original All Blacks</a> for the 5th game of their tour, despite losing 28-0 the club made an impression as four Tigers were called up by England for their test with the New Zealanders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Allegations_of_professionalism">Allegations of professionalism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leicester_Tigers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Allegations of professionalism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:362px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1908_JohnJackett_FredJackson_TomSmith_portraits_from_Anglo_Welsh_tour_to_New_Zealand.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="200" data-file-width="470" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/1908_JohnJackett_FredJackson_TomSmith_portraits_from_Anglo_Welsh_tour_to_New_Zealand.jpg/360px-1908_JohnJackett_FredJackson_TomSmith_portraits_from_Anglo_Welsh_tour_to_New_Zealand.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/a/a4/1908_JohnJackett_FredJackson_TomSmith_portraits_from_Anglo_Welsh_tour_to_New_Zealand.jpg 1.5x" width="360"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1908_JohnJackett_FredJackson_TomSmith_portraits_from_Anglo_Welsh_tour_to_New_Zealand.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Tour portraits of Smith, Jackson and Jackett</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1908 the club had three players selected for the <a href="/wiki/1908_British_Lions_tour_to_New_Zealand_and_Australia" title="1908 British Lions tour to New Zealand and Australia">1908 Anglo-Welsh tour of New Zealand</a>. <a href="/wiki/Edward_Jackett" title="Edward Jackett">John Jackett</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_William_Smith" title="Thomas William Smith">Tom Smith</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Stanley_Jackson" title="Frederick Stanley Jackson">Fred Jackson</a> became the first Tigers selected for an overseas tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Controversy dogged Jackson; a secretive man it was claimed he had played for <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Football_League" title="Rugby Football League">Northern Union</a> side <a href="/wiki/Swinton_Lions" title="Swinton Lions">Swinton</a> under the name "John Jones", such a charge was serious as it could have not only professionalised Jackson but all those who had associations with him. Jackson was withdrawn from the tour and settled in New Zealand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>Allegations of veiled professionalism were levied at Leicester during the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Football_Union" title="Rugby Football Union">RFU</a>'s 1908 <a href="/wiki/Annual_general_meeting" title="Annual general meeting">AGM</a> and an inquiry ordered, though a vote to expel Leicester from the RFU was defeated. The inquiry was not only into professionalism but also the transfers of Jackson &amp; Jackett as well as <a href="/wiki/Alf_Kewney" title="Alf Kewney">Alf Kewney</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Hogarth_(rugby_union)" title="Thomas Hogarth (rugby union)">Tom Hogarth</a>. On 30 January 1909, the day Leicester hosted an <a href="/wiki/England_national_rugby_union_team" title="England national rugby union team">England</a> v <a href="/wiki/France_national_rugby_union_team" title="France national rugby union team">France</a> test match, the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Football_Union" title="Rugby Football Union">RFU</a> announced the outcome of the inquiry clearing the club on all charges in what has been described as a <a href="/wiki/Whitewashing_(censorship)" title="Whitewashing (censorship)">whitewash</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>As if to refute the notion that the Tigers were made up purely of imported players there were 12 locals selected for the 1909 Midland Counties Cup Final against <a href="/wiki/Coventry_R.F.C." title="Coventry R.F.C.">Coventry</a>. Tigers won the cup, the first time they had entered after a four-year absence, 8-3 with two tries from <a href="/wiki/Percy_Lawrie_(rugby_union)" title="Percy Lawrie (rugby union)">Percy Lawrie</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>December 1909 saw the beginning of a cherished tradition as Tigers played the <a href="/wiki/Barbarian_F.C." title="Barbarian F.C.">Barbarians</a> for the first time, holding them to a 9-9 draw. The fixture became a vital feature in the club's calendar delivering large attendances until open professionalism and league rugby in the 1990s forced it to gradually be abandoned due to fixture congestion.</p>
<p>Tigers won the Midlands Counties Cup 3 more times in 4 years to cement their place as the midland's premier side before the outbreak of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_World_War" title="First World War">war</a> in 1914.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="War_and_reconstruction_of_Welford_Road">War and reconstruction of Welford Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leicester_Tigers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: War and reconstruction of Welford Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>With <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">war</a> declared the Leicester committee suspended matches on 3 September 1914. Two charity matches were played against the <a href="/wiki/Barbarian_F.C." title="Barbarian F.C.">Barbarians</a> in 1915 but otherwise Tigers played no rugby for the duration of the war. 17 players from the club lost their lives during the war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>Within 6 weeks of the <a href="/wiki/Armistice_of_11_November_1918" title="Armistice of 11 November 1918">Armistice</a> being signed Tigers were playing their first game, facing the 4th battalion of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Leicestershire_Regiment" title="Royal Leicestershire Regiment">Leicestershire Regiment</a> in what was also the official opening of the Members Stand on the north side of the ground.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>Tigers enjoyed their first full season back; winger Teddy Haselmere scored a club record 59 tries, no man before or since has even reached 40. At this time formations were not set in the way they are now and Tigers regularly played with 7 forwards and 8 backs, meaning overlaps for the wingers were plentiful.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <i>New Stand</i> (later renamed the <i>Crumbie Stand</i> in honour of Tom Crumbie) costing £21,000 (approx £850,000 in 2016) was officially opened on 2 October 1920 before a match against <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Carnegie" title="Yorkshire Carnegie">Headingley</a> by the President of the RFU Ernest Prescott, Tigers celebrated with a 33-3 victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>Terracing was added in front of the new stand the next season and the Members Stand extended to give Welford Road a seated capacity of 10,250. Subscriptions for stand seats was 25 shillings (£50 in 2016 money) and unemployed men gained free entry to the end terraces on production of their out of work card.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> These ground developments lead to attendances that would not be bettered until the 2000s as 20,000 fans watched the loss to <a href="/wiki/Newport_RFC" title="Newport RFC">Newport</a> on 29 October 1921.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourists_in_the_20s_and_the_death_of_Tom_Crumbie">Tourists in the 20s and the death of Tom Crumbie</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leicester_Tigers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Tourists in the 20s and the death of Tom Crumbie">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:362px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Racing-Leicester-1923.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1054" data-file-width="1421" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Racing-Leicester-1923.jpg/360px-Racing-Leicester-1923.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Racing-Leicester-1923.jpg/540px-Racing-Leicester-1923.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Racing-Leicester-1923.jpg/720px-Racing-Leicester-1923.jpg 2x" width="360"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Racing-Leicester-1923.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Leicester's return match against Racing in February 1923</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Leicester welcomed their first <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">French</a> visitors on 28 December 1922 when <a href="/wiki/Racing_92" title="Racing 92">Racing club de France</a> formed part of Tigers' Christmas festival, the hosts winning 4-0 thanks to a Haselmere drop goal. Tigers returned the visit in February 1923 but lost 19-9 despite scoring three tries.</p>
<p>The visit of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1924-25_New_Zealand_rugby_union_tour_of_Britain,_Ireland_and_France" title="1924-25 New Zealand rugby union tour of Britain, Ireland and France">Invincible All Blacks</a> on 4 October 1924 saw a record attendance at Welford Road of 35,000 that stands to this day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Tigers were beaten 27-0 by the tourists but good things were still to come that season as <a href="/wiki/Leicestershire_Rugby_Union" title="Leicestershire Rugby Union">Leicestershire</a> won their only <a href="/wiki/County_Championship_(rugby_union)" title="County Championship (rugby union)">County Championship</a> against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gloucestershire_Rugby_Union" title="Gloucestershire Rugby Union">Gloucestershire</a> with the entire starting XV coming from the Tigers.</p>
<p>The next season saw a visit by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1926-27_New_Zealand_Maori_rugby_union_tour" title="1926-27 New Zealand Maori rugby union tour">New Zealand Maori</a> and a closer result, Tigers leading at half time 8-3 thanks to a try from Ewert Farndon and 5 points from the boot of <a href="/wiki/Doug_Prentice" title="Doug Prentice">Doug Prentice</a> but eventually succumbing 15-13 to the Maori tourists.</p>
<p>In the 1926–27 season Leicester started using letters to identify their forwards; <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_Post" title="Birmingham Post"><i>The Birmingham Post</i></a> report for the match against <a href="/wiki/Bath_Rugby" title="Bath Rugby">Bath</a> on 6 October 1926 noted "Leicester's forwards were picked out easily as their jerseys were decorated with large bold letters A-G",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> expanding the practice by 1931–32 to the whole team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>Tom Crumbie died on 13 March 1928, he was described as the cog around which the club functioned and contemporary reports say he epitomised the club. Tigers wore black armbands for their next fixture against <a href="/wiki/Penarth_RFC" title="Penarth RFC">Penarth</a>. On 4 April the club appointed his successor Eric Thorneloe and six months later renamed <i>The New Stand</i> as <i>The Crumbie Stand</i> in honour of Crumbie.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_honours_as_club.27s_fortunes_wane">Personal honours as club's fortunes wane</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leicester_Tigers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Personal honours as club's fortunes wane">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Club captain <a href="/wiki/Doug_Prentice" title="Doug Prentice">Doug Prentice</a> was given the honour of captaining the <a href="/wiki/1930_British_Lions_tour_to_New_Zealand_and_Australia" title="1930 British Lions tour to New Zealand and Australia">1930 British Lions tour to New Zealand and Australia</a>, alongside two Leicester team mates <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Kendrew" title="Douglas Kendrew">Joe Kendrew</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_Beamish" title="George Beamish">George Beamish</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Irish forward <a href="/wiki/George_Beamish" title="George Beamish">Beamish</a> played 21 games on the tour, the most of any player, and is credited with introducing the green of <a href="/wiki/Ireland_national_rugby_union_team" title="Ireland national rugby union team">Ireland</a> into the <a href="/wiki/British_and_Irish_Lions" title="British and Irish Lions">Lions</a> playing kit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Misc2_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Misc2-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>No doubt the presence of such star players lead the next season to the first <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> radio broadcast of a Tigers game. The match against <a href="/wiki/Waterloo_FC" title="Waterloo FC">Waterloo</a> on 29 November 1930 was the first radio broadcast of a Leicester game; Tigers won 21-5.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Great Depression in the United Kingdom">Great Depression</a> hit the club's gates hard. With no cup or league competitions attendances for friendly fixtures tumbled to a low of 346 against <a href="/wiki/Bridgwater_%26_Albion" title="Bridgwater &amp; Albion">Bridgwater Albion</a> in 1934.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> It took the introduction of leagues in the 1980s before crowd numbers returned to their pre-depression level. The club's poor finances meant an invitation by <a href="/wiki/Amatori_Rugby_Milano" title="Amatori Rugby Milano">Amatori Milano</a> to tour <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> had to be declined.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>Personal honours for the players masked some of the decline though. <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Gadney" title="Bernard Gadney">Bernard Gadney</a> became the club's first home produced England captain in 1934 and was captain when four Leicester players were part of the first <a href="/wiki/England_national_rugby_union_team" title="England national rugby union team">England</a> side to beat the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1935-36_New_Zealand_rugby_union_tour_of_Britain,_Ireland_and_Canada" title="1935-36 New Zealand rugby union tour of Britain, Ireland and Canada">All Blacks</a>. Tigers winger <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Obolensky" title="Alexander Obolensky">Alexander Obolensky</a> scored two tries on debut in the 13-0 win. Gadney also became the club's second player to captain the <a href="/wiki/British_and_Irish_Lions" title="British and Irish Lions">British Lions</a> on their <a href="/wiki/1936_British_Lions_tour_to_Argentina" title="1936 British Lions tour to Argentina">tour to Argentina</a> where he was joined by Obolensky and <a href="/wiki/Charles_Beamish" title="Charles Beamish">Charles Beamish</a>.</p>
<p>1936-37 was the worst season since 1889-90 for the club with only 14 wins from 39 matches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Results picked up slightly the next two season before the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_World_War" title="Second World War">Second World War</a> intervened and regularly fixtures were abandoned for the next 5 years. 26 Tigers players lost their lives in the war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post_War_move_away_from_invitation_side">Post War move away from invitation side</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leicester_Tigers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Post War move away from invitation side">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Fifteen days after <a href="/wiki/Victory_in_Europe_Day" title="Victory in Europe Day">VE Day</a> the club's committee held their first meeting to determine the future of the club. The roof of the Crumbie Stand had been damaged in air raids, there was a collapsed wall at the Welford Road end and significant repairs to the clubhouse were required where the Army had bored holes into the floor. The club ran two teams that year; the First XV and Leicestershire Harlequins, named for the war-time side that provided rugby for locals on leave or passing servicemen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Harlequins were quickly changed to be an "A XV", the first time the club had run more than one side for 40 years. The decision was unpopular with the junior clubs that provided the bulk of the players for the side. It ran for ten seasons until being discontinued in 1955.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1947 local winger <a href="/wiki/Harry_Sibson" title="Harry Sibson">Harry Sibson</a> joined from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aylestonians" title="Aylestonians">Aylestonians</a> and went on to play 183 games. Sibson is credited for the introduction of a new offside law at scrums. Sibson fulfilled many roles including club secretary and club president.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>Tigers first televised game by the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> was on 3 February 1951 when they beat <a href="/wiki/London_Scottish_F.C." title="London Scottish F.C.">London Scottish</a> 14-0 at the <a href="/wiki/Athletic_Ground,_Richmond" title="Athletic Ground, Richmond">Richmond Athletic Ground</a>; earlier that year Tigers had refused a request to televise the Barbarians game fearing it might affect the gate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Romania_national_rugby_union_team" title="Romania national rugby union team">Romania</a> became the first international side to face Tigers for 25 years when they played on 8 September 1956. The game ended a 6-6 draw.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>The club underwent a significant restructure in the 1956/57 season. The practice of being an "invitation" club featuring only a First XV was to stop and Tigers were to adopt a more traditional membership club based approach with multiple sides. The "A XV" was to be re-introduced under the name "Extra First XV" with a third "Colts XV" also formed. With only on side the club had been suffering losing players because of a lack of regular rugby for those on the fringes of the starting side. Eric Thorneloe retired from his role of secretary at the end of the season giving the feel that this was the end of an era.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Matthews.27_team_breaks_record_and_White_appointed_coach">Matthews' team breaks record and White appointed coach</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leicester_Tigers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Matthews' team breaks record and White appointed coach">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1959 <a href="/wiki/Tony_O%27Reilly" title="Tony O'Reilly">Tony O'Reilly</a> and <a href="/wiki/Phil_Horrocks-Taylor" title="Phil Horrocks-Taylor">Phil Horrocks-Taylor</a> were selected for the <a href="/wiki/1959_British_Lions_tour_to_Australia_and_New_Zealand" title="1959 British Lions tour to Australia and New Zealand">1959 British Lions tour to Australia and New Zealand</a>, the first since <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Gadney" title="Bernard Gadney">Gadney</a> 23 years earlier. Horrocks-Taylor's influence is best shown by the 1960-61 season where the club won 17 of 22 matches with him in the side and only 7 of 20 without.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>The 1963-64 season saw 26 wins the most in 29 seasons but attendances were poor, only three games were watched by more than a thousand people and even the Barbarians fixture drew only 4,284.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> The season also saw <a href="/wiki/David_Matthews_(rugby_union)" title="David Matthews (rugby union)">David Matthews</a> set the record for most consecutive appearances for the club with 109.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/David_Matthews_(rugby_union)" title="David Matthews (rugby union)">Matthews</a> was to become captain in 1965 and in 1966/67 lead the club to a record 33 wins. The previous record had stood at 31 games since 1898.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Chalkie_White_(rugby_player)" title="Chalkie White (rugby player)">Chalkie White</a> became coach in 1968; the same season Tom Berry became Leicester's first President of the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Football_Union" title="Rugby Football Union">RFU</a>. White combined with captain Graham Willars to reform Tigers play in light of rule changes that summer which banned kicking directly to touch from outside your own 25 yard area and drastically reduced kicking. Tigers scored 122 tries and 657 points that season. Moves towards a return to competitive rugby were made with discussion held on leagues or a knock out cup. Tigers president Nick Hughes favoured regional pools before a national knock out tournament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>Despite usually returning more wins than losses Leicester's standing at the time was not what it is now. Coventry had not been beaten for 16 years for instance, and international honours were limited.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Introduction_of_the_National_Cup_and_first_Youth_side">Introduction of the National Cup and first Youth side</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leicester_Tigers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Introduction of the National Cup and first Youth side">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>1970/71 saw <a href="/wiki/Peter_Wheeler_(rugby_union)" title="Peter Wheeler (rugby union)">Peter Wheeler</a> emerge as first choice hooker having made his debut the year before, he ended the season on <a href="/wiki/1971_England_rugby_union_tour_of_Far_East" title="1971 England rugby union tour of Far East">England's tour to the Far East</a>. Attendance for the annual <a href="/wiki/Barbarian_F.C." title="Barbarian F.C.">Barbarians</a> game hit a nadir with a crowd of only 2,518.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>The 1971/72 season saw changes which, over time, would radically change both the club and the game. The <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Football_Union" title="Rugby Football Union">RFU</a> introduced for the first time a national <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1971-72_John_Player_Cup" title="1971-72 John Player Cup">Knockout Cup</a> competition for clubs and on 16 November 1971 Tigers played their first competitive cup match since 1914, a 10-3 defeat to <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_R.F.C." title="Nottingham R.F.C.">Nottingham</a> at their Beeston ground.</p>
<p>Also introduced that season was Tigers' first "Youth" XV, based on the Leicester Ravens a collection of the best 14 and 15 year olds in the county. Their first game was on 15 April 1972 and they made an immediate impact, captain of that side was Steve Kenney who would score the winning try in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1978-79_John_Player_Cup" title="1978-79 John Player Cup">1979 Cup Final</a>. Only six year later <a href="/wiki/Paul_Dodge" title="Paul Dodge">Paul Dodge</a> became the first graduate to win an international cap.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>Tigers attack was going from strength to strength recording their highest yet points total for a season in both 1971/72, 789, and in 1972/73 scoring 988 points. The previous record set in 1919/20 was 756. But defence was an issue conceding 40 points to both <a href="/wiki/Coventry_R.F.C." title="Coventry R.F.C.">Coventry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bath_Rugby" title="Bath Rugby">Bath</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Tigers reached the quarter finals of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1972-73_John_Player_Cup" title="1972-73 John Player Cup">Cup in 1973</a>.</p>
<p>11 September 1973 saw Tigers beat the touring <a href="/wiki/Fiji_national_rugby_union_team" title="Fiji national rugby union team">Fijian national team</a> 22-17 in front of a 12,000 crowd and on 3 October beat touring Australian <a href="/wiki/Shute_Shield" title="Shute Shield">Shute Shield</a> champions <a href="/wiki/Randwick_DRUFC" title="Randwick DRUFC">Randwick</a> 15-10. There was still no joy in the Cup with a first round defeat to <a href="/wiki/Northampton_Saints" title="Northampton Saints">Northampton</a> also meaning Tigers failed to qualify the next season. Tigers fly half <a href="/wiki/Alan_Old" title="Alan Old">Alan Old</a> started for England as they beat <a href="/wiki/1973_England_rugby_union_tour_of_Fiji_and_New_Zealand" title="1973 England rugby union tour of Fiji and New Zealand">New Zealand in New Zealand</a> for the first time<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> and then beat Australia at <a href="/wiki/Twickenham_Stadium" title="Twickenham Stadium">Twickenham</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cup_success">Cup success</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leicester_Tigers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Cup success">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Tigers were not involved in the 1974-75 Cup and lost in the 1st round of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1975-76_John_Player_Cup" title="1975-76 John Player Cup">1975-76 Cup</a> to Liverpool. This forced the club into the Midlands qualifiers for the only time. They beat <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_R.F.C." title="Nottingham R.F.C.">Nottingham</a>, local junior club <a href="/wiki/Leicester_Lions_RFC" title="Leicester Lions RFC">Westleigh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kettering_Rugby_Football_Club" title="Kettering Rugby Football Club">Kettering</a> to qualify for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1976-77_John_Player_Cup" title="1976-77 John Player Cup">1976-77 Cup</a> where a win against <a href="/wiki/Wakefield_RFC" title="Wakefield RFC">Wakefield</a> lead to a second round defeat against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moseley_Rugby_Football_Club" title="Moseley Rugby Football Club">Moseley</a>.</p>
<p>This era saw a huge increase in the popularity of the <a href="/wiki/Barbarian_F.C." title="Barbarian F.C.">Barbarians</a> annual fixture which crowds of 15,000 in 1973 &amp; 1975, 17,000 in 1974 and 21,000 in 1976. This contrasted with usual crowds in the low hundreds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>1976-77 saw the introduction of regional "Merit Tables" by the RFU, the first step on the road to full leagues. Based around traditional fixtures Tigers faced <a href="/wiki/Bedford_Blues" title="Bedford Blues">Bedford</a>, Birmingham, <a href="/wiki/Coventry_R.F.C." title="Coventry R.F.C.">Coventry</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moseley_Rugby_Football_Club" title="Moseley Rugby Football Club">Moseley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northampton_Saints" title="Northampton Saints">Northampton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nuneaton_R.F.C." title="Nuneaton R.F.C.">Nuneaton</a>, Nottingham and <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Lions" title="Rugby Lions">Rugby</a> in the Midlands Merit Table finishing second to Moseley with a record of played 8 won 6.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>It took 6 years before Leicester were drawn at home in the cup but in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1977-78_John_Player_Cup" title="1977-78 John Player Cup">1977-78</a> they received four in a row beating <a href="/wiki/Hartlepool_Rovers" title="Hartlepool Rovers">Hartlepool Rovers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rosslyn_Park_F.C." title="Rosslyn Park F.C.">Rosslyn Park</a>, Northampton and Coventry on their way to a first <a href="/wiki/Twickenham_Stadium" title="Twickenham Stadium">Twickenham</a> final against <a href="/wiki/Gloucester_Rugby" title="Gloucester Rugby">Gloucester</a>. The game ended in a 6-3 loss to the Cherry and Whites; the attendance was 25,282 more than double the previous season. Cup success also coincided with Tigers membership more than doubling from 750 in 1978 to 2,000 by the end of 1979.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>Home cup draws continued the next season as Northampton (29-3) and <a href="/wiki/Broughton_Park_RUFC" title="Broughton Park RUFC">Broughton Park</a> (30-7) were beaten at Welford Road. Bedford were beaten at Goldington Road in the quarter finals before <a href="/wiki/Wasps_RFC" title="Wasps RFC">Wasps</a> were defeated 43-7 in the semi finals. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1978-79_John_Player_Cup" title="1978-79 John Player Cup">The final</a> was against perennial rivals Moseley and Steve Kenney scored with three minutes remaining to win it 15-12 for Leicester.</p>
<p>Tigers retained the cup in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1979-80_John_Player_Cup" title="1979-80 John Player Cup">1979-80</a> beating <a href="/wiki/Orrell_R.U.F.C." title="Orrell R.U.F.C.">Orrell</a> (16-7), Moseley (17-7), <a href="/wiki/London_Scottish_F.C." title="London Scottish F.C.">London Scottish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Harlequin_F.C." title="Harlequin F.C.">Harlequins</a> in the early rounds before beating <a href="/wiki/London_Irish" title="London Irish">London Irish</a> 21–9 in the final at Twickenham in front of a record crowd of 27,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> 1979-80 also saw Tigers win the Midlands Merit Table for the first time with a record played 7 games and won 6 and provide four players in <a href="/wiki/1980_Five_Nations_Championship" title="1980 Five Nations Championship">England's grandslam of 1980</a>. <a href="/wiki/Clive_Woodward" title="Clive Woodward">Clive Woodward</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peter_Wheeler_(rugby_union)" title="Peter Wheeler (rugby union)">Peter Wheeler</a> were selected for the <a href="/wiki/1980_British_Lions_tour_to_South_Africa" title="1980 British Lions tour to South Africa">1980 British Lions tour to South Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Dodge" title="Paul Dodge">Paul Dodge</a> joined them as an injury replacement and all three were selected for the third test defeat against the <a href="/wiki/South_Africa_national_rugby_union_team" title="South Africa national rugby union team">Springboks</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Centenary">Centenary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leicester_Tigers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Centenary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>To celebrate the club's centenary a 6 match tour to <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a> was arranged in August 1980, the first undertaken by an English club in the southern hemisphere. Tigers lost 22-12 to <a href="/wiki/Queensland_Reds" title="Queensland Reds">Queensland</a> in their first match but recorded victories over <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Suburbs_RUFC" title="Eastern Suburbs RUFC">Eastern Suburbs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Randwick_DRUFC" title="Randwick DRUFC">Randwick</a> before traveling to Fiji and winning 3 games.</p>
<p>Prestige fixtures staged at Welford Road to mark the centenary were the visit of the <a href="/wiki/Ireland_Wolfhounds" title="Ireland Wolfhounds">Irish Wolfhounds</a> who were beaten 10-6; <a href="/wiki/Romania_national_rugby_union_team" title="Romania national rugby union team">Romania</a> who won 39-7, with <a href="/wiki/Floric%C4%83_Murariu" title="Florică Murariu">Florică Murariu</a> scoring 4 tries for the visitors and a return visit from <a href="/wiki/Queensland_Reds" title="Queensland Reds">Queensland</a> who were beaten 21-9.</p>
<p>Tigers retained the Midlands Merit Table title in November with an undefeated record of played 7, won 6, drawn 1. On 25 April 1981 Tigers traveled to Moseley where <a href="/wiki/Dusty_Hare" title="Dusty Hare">Dusty Hare</a> broke the world record for points scored in first class fixtures. His total of 3,658 over took the previous record held by Moseley's own <a href="/wiki/Sam_Doble" title="Sam Doble">Sam Doble</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>The cup was won again in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1980-81_John_Player_Cup" title="1980-81 John Player Cup">1980-81</a>. Roundhay, <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Rugby" title="Bristol Rugby">Bristol</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sale_Sharks" title="Sale Sharks">Sale</a> were beaten in the early rounds; <a href="/wiki/London_Scottish_F.C." title="London Scottish F.C.">London Scottish</a> in the semi finals became the first cup game to go to extra time before <a href="/wiki/Les_Cusworth" title="Les Cusworth">Les Cusworth</a> kicked two drop goals to seal a fourth successive trip to Twickenham. Leicester scored three tries to beat <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_Falcons" title="Newcastle Falcons">Gosforth</a> 22–15. This meant they were allowed to keep the trophy.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1980s_to_the_beginning_of_league_rugby">1980s to the beginning of league rugby</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leicester_Tigers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: 1980s to the beginning of league rugby">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the early 1980s league rugby was still a controversial idea when proposed by an RFU report in 1980 and met with mixed reaction honorary secretary Jerry Day foreseeing that "If a club wanted to compete .. in a league system it would have to become almost professional", whilst <a href="/wiki/Peter_Wheeler_(rugby_union)" title="Peter Wheeler (rugby union)">Wheeler</a> thought leagues "long overdue".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>Tigers 18 match unbeaten run the cup was over in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1981-82_John_Player_Cup" title="1981-82 John Player Cup">1982</a> when the club lost to Moseley in the semi finals, the club wasn't to win the cup again until 1993 though there were finals in 1983 &amp; 1989. This was also <a href="/wiki/Chalkie_White_(rugby_player)" title="Chalkie White (rugby player)">Chalkie White</a>'s last season with the club after 30 years as a player, administrator or coach.</p>
<p>In 1981 Tigers played <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1981-82_Australia_rugby_union_tour_of_Britain_and_Ireland" title="1981-82 Australia rugby union tour of Britain and Ireland">Australia</a> leading until the 78th minute only to lose 18-15;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> this was the first visit by one of the three major southern hemisphere nations since 1924.</p>
<p>A new generation of players who were to shape the club made their debuts in the early '80s; <a href="/wiki/Dean_Richards_(rugby_union)" title="Dean Richards (rugby union)">Dean Richards</a> in 1982 against <a href="/wiki/Neath_RFC" title="Neath RFC">Neath</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Wells_(rugby_union)" title="John Wells (rugby union)">John Wells</a> in 1983 against <a href="/wiki/Harlequin_F.C." title="Harlequin F.C.">Harlequins</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rory_Underwood" title="Rory Underwood">Rory Underwood</a> in 1983 against Birmingham.</p>
<p>Seven Leicester players were part of the Midlands side which defeated the <a href="/wiki/1983_New_Zealand_rugby_union_tour_of_Scotland_and_England" title="1983 New Zealand rugby union tour of Scotland and England">All Blacks</a> 19-13 at Welford Road in November 1983, with six player including captain <a href="/wiki/Peter_Wheeler_(rugby_union)" title="Peter Wheeler (rugby union)">Peter Wheeler</a> named in the <a href="/wiki/England_national_rugby_union_team" title="England national rugby union team">England</a> side that also beat the tourists 15-9 at Twickenham.</p>
<p>Off the field the club were beginning to develop commercially, singing a 5-year sponsorship with brewers <a href="/wiki/Allied_Breweries" title="Allied Breweries">Ind Coope</a> in 1984.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1985 the penultimate step towards league rugby was taken as the <a href="/wiki/John_Smith%27s_Brewery" title="John Smith's Brewery">John Smith's</a> Merit Table A was launched. It was a national competition that featured the best sides from the four regional merit tables but was still based on old traditional fixtures; Tigers played 10 counting games in the first season whilst <a href="/wiki/Harlequin_F.C." title="Harlequin F.C.">Harlequins</a> played only 4.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> The national merit tables ran for two season with the table based on win percentage to take account of the different numbers of games played; <a href="/wiki/Gloucester_Rugby" title="Gloucester Rugby">Gloucester</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bath_Rugby" title="Bath Rugby">Bath</a> each topped the table once, Tigers finished 4th and 2nd.</p>
<p>League rugby was finally launched in England in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1987-88_Courage_League" title="1987-88 Courage League">1987</a>. The main difference from the merit table was all sides would now have to play all other sides in a round robin, though a fixtures dispute meant the Tigers v Gloucester match was not played. Tigers hit the top of the league on 28 November following a 21-3 win away at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moseley_R.F.C." title="Moseley R.F.C.">Moseley</a> and stayed there losing only one match all season. When they beat <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Waterloo_R.F.C." title="Waterloo R.F.C.">Waterloo</a> in front of 7,130 supporters on the last day of the <a href="/wiki/1987%E2%80%9388_Courage_League" title="1987–88 Courage League">1987-88 season</a>, Easter Monday 4 April, the Tigers became England's first official champions.</p>
<p>Tigers finished the season on 37 points, one ahead of nearest rivals <a href="/wiki/Wasps_RFC" title="Wasps RFC">Wasps</a>.</p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1988-89_Courage_League" title="1988-89 Courage League">1988-89 Courage League</a> saw Tigers slump to 6th in the league, their joint worst ever finish, but more joy was to be had in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1988-89_Pilkington_Cup" title="1988-89 Pilkington Cup">Cup</a> as Tigers beat Liverpool St Helens (37-6), Rosslyn Park (23-9), Wasps (22-18) and Quins (16-7) to set up a final with Bath. In what was <a href="/wiki/Dusty_Hare" title="Dusty Hare">Dusty Hare</a>'s 394th and last game for the club Tigers lead 6-0 at half time but lost 10-6 with <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Barnes" title="Stuart Barnes">Stuart Barnes</a> scoring Bath's winning try in the 78th minute.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Martin_Johnson_(rugby_union)" title="Martin Johnson (rugby union)">Martin Johnson</a> made his debut for the First XV in February 1989 whilst <a href="/wiki/Les_Cusworth" title="Les Cusworth">Les Cusworth</a> retired at the end of the 1989/90 season. In August 1990 Leicester appointed their first paid official: Tony Russ, who had led <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saracen_F.C." title="Saracen F.C.">Saracens</a> to promotion then 4th place in the league before accepting the role of "Director of Coaching" at Leicester.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Neil_Back" title="Neil Back">Neil Back</a> joined that summer and made his debut at home against <a href="/wiki/Bedford_Blues" title="Bedford Blues">Bedford</a>, whist <a href="/wiki/Graham_Rowntree" title="Graham Rowntree">Graham Rowntree</a> was promoted from the club's youth ranks and made his debut in October against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oxford_University" title="Oxford University">Oxford University</a>. The changing of the guard from Cup winning team of the early 80s was complete when <a href="/wiki/Paul_Dodge" title="Paul Dodge">Paul Dodge</a> retired at the end of the 1990/91 season.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nineties_and_Dean_Richards_era">Nineties and Dean Richards era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leicester_Tigers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Nineties and Dean Richards era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The early 1990s saw the emergence of Leicester's renowned ABC Club, so called because of the letters the front row players wore on their shirts; <a href="/wiki/Graham_Rowntree" title="Graham Rowntree">Graham Rowntree</a> played loosehead and wore "A", hooker <a href="/wiki/Richard_Cockerill" title="Richard Cockerill">Richard Cockerill</a> wore "B" and <a href="/wiki/Darren_Garforth" title="Darren Garforth">Darren Garforth</a> played tighthead prop and wore "C". The trio started 166 games together between 1992 and 2002, Garforth and Rowntree started another 72 games together at prop, but with different hookers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>Leicester began one of the greatest winning streaks of any team. This streak started when a young pack helped Leicester to defeat <a href="/wiki/Harlequin_F.C." title="Harlequin F.C.">Harlequins</a> 23–16 in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1992-93_Pilkington_Cup" title="1992-93 Pilkington Cup">1993 cup final</a>. They were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1994-95_English_Premiership_(rugby_union)" title="1994-95 English Premiership (rugby union)">English champions again in 1995</a>, beat <a href="/wiki/Sale_Sharks" title="Sale Sharks">Sale</a> 9-3 in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1996-97_Pilkington_Cup" title="1996-97 Pilkington Cup">1997 Pilkington Cup Final</a> and were the first English team to get to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heineken_Cup" title="Heineken Cup">Heineken Cup</a> <a href="/wiki/1997_Heineken_Cup_Final" title="1997 Heineken Cup Final">final</a> before losing to <a href="/wiki/CA_Brive" title="CA Brive">Brive</a> in the same year. In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1995-96_Pilkington_Cup" title="1995-96 Pilkington Cup">1996 cup final</a>, Tigers lost to Bath (who was just finishing its own great domination of English rugby) after referee Steve Lander gave a contentious penalty try in the last minute which sealed their victory. After the match <a href="/wiki/Neil_Back" title="Neil Back">Neil Back</a> pushed over Lander landing himself a six-month ban.</p>
<p>From 1999 to 2002, under the captaincy of <a href="/wiki/Martin_Johnson_(rugby_union)" title="Martin Johnson (rugby union)">Martin Johnson</a> and the management of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dean_Richards_(rugby_player)" title="Dean Richards (rugby player)">Dean Richards</a>, who became Director of Rugby for the club in February 1998, they won four consecutive Premiership titles and the first Zürich Championship play-offs,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> bringing their total of league championships to six — tied with Bath for most wins.</p>
<p>On 28 August 1999 a record ten Tigers were capped for England in the <a href="/wiki/1999_Rugby_World_Cup" title="1999 Rugby World Cup">World Cup</a> warm up game against <a href="/wiki/Canada_national_rugby_union_team" title="Canada national rugby union team">Canada</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>They also won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heineken_Cup" title="Heineken Cup">Heineken Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/2001_Heineken_Cup_Final" title="2001 Heineken Cup Final">2001</a> and <a href="/wiki/2002_Heineken_Cup_Final" title="2002 Heineken Cup Final">2002</a> — Leicester defeated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stade_Fran%C3%A7ais_Paris" title="Stade Français Paris">Stade Français</a> (34–30) in 2001, and <a href="/wiki/Munster_Rugby" title="Munster Rugby">Munster</a> (15–9) in 2002.</p>
<p>Leicester during this time had a very good home record; they went 57 games unbeaten at home in a period that stretched from 30 December 1997 to 30 November 2002 and included 52 successive wins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> During these four seasons Leicester lost only 14 games out of the 92 they played.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2003_Rugby_World_Cup" title="2003 Rugby World Cup">2003 Rugby World Cup</a>, the club had seven representatives in the winning <a href="/wiki/England_national_rugby_union_team" title="England national rugby union team">England</a> squad: <a href="/wiki/Martin_Johnson_(rugby_union)" title="Martin Johnson (rugby union)">Martin Johnson</a> (captain), <a href="/wiki/Neil_Back" title="Neil Back">Neil Back</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martin_Corry_(rugby_union)" title="Martin Corry (rugby union)">Martin Corry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ben_Kay" title="Ben Kay">Ben Kay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Moody" title="Lewis Moody">Lewis Moody</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dorian_West" title="Dorian West">Dorian West</a> and <a href="/wiki/Julian_White" title="Julian White">Julian White</a>. However while these players were away Leicester's form suffered, even with the returning players they were knocked out of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2002-03_Heineken_Cup" title="2002-03 Heineken Cup">that season's Heineken Cup</a> in the group stages and were 12 points away from Heineken Cup qualification for the next season with 8 games remaining when they decided to sack <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dean_Richards_(rugby_player)" title="Dean Richards (rugby player)">Dean Richards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post_Richards_era">Post Richards era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leicester_Tigers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Post Richards era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tom_Croft_2012.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="780" data-file-width="746" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tom_Croft_2012.jpg/230px-Tom_Croft_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tom_Croft_2012.jpg/345px-Tom_Croft_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tom_Croft_2012.jpg/460px-Tom_Croft_2012.jpg 2x" width="230"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tom_Croft_2012.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Tom Croft made his debut in 2006 after coming though the club's academy</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After Richards' departure Tigers turned to his assistant coach <a href="/wiki/John_Wells_(rugby_union)" title="John Wells (rugby union)">John Wells</a> as temporary cover. Wells' tenure saw Tigers fortunes improve and Heineken Cup qualification for the next season secured. He was named as Richards' permanent successor on 28 April 2004 whilst <a href="/wiki/Pat_Howard" title="Pat Howard">Pat Howard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Cockerill" title="Richard Cockerill">Richard Cockerill</a> were announced as his assistant coaches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/John_Wells_(rugby_union)" title="John Wells (rugby union)">John Wells</a>' first full season in charge of the team Leicester finished the regular season top of the league, also progressing to the semi-final of the Heineken cup before defeat to Toulouse at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Walkers_Stadium" title="Walkers Stadium">Walkers Stadium</a>. In Martin Johnson and Neil Back's last game for Leicester they lost the Premiership Final to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/London_Wasps" title="London Wasps">Wasps</a>. After this game John Wells left Leicester to take up a position in the RFU's coaching academy,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> eventually rising to England forwards coach.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> He was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Pat_Howard" title="Pat Howard">Pat Howard</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2005–06, the Tigers finished second to the <a href="/wiki/Sale_Sharks" title="Sale Sharks">Sale Sharks</a> in the league before losing to the same team in the Premiership final. They again proceeded to the knockout stages of the Heineken Cup, again they lost at the Walkers Stadium to Bath. In the new <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Welsh_Cup" title="Anglo-Welsh Cup">Anglo-Welsh Cup</a> Leicester won their group but lost in the semi-finals to Wasps at the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Stadium" title="Millennium Stadium">Millennium Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cardiff" title="Cardiff">Cardiff</a>, Wales.</p>
<p>Over the summer of 2006 the core of a new pack was recruited especially <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jordan_Crane_(rugby_player)" title="Jordan Crane (rugby player)">Jordan Crane</a>, the Number 8, who arrived from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leeds_Carnegie" title="Leeds Carnegie">Leeds</a>; <a href="/wiki/Martin_Castrogiovanni" title="Martin Castrogiovanni">Martin Castrogiovanni</a> joined from <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Calvisano" title="Rugby Calvisano">Calvisano</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marcos_Ayerza" title="Marcos Ayerza">Marcos Ayerza</a> joined from domestic rugby in his native Argentina. <a href="/wiki/Tom_Croft" title="Tom Croft">Tom Croft</a> also made his debut this season after coming through the club's academy system.</p>
<p>Leicester won their first piece of silverware for five years on 15 April 2007, beating the <a href="/wiki/Ospreys_(rugby_team)" title="Ospreys (rugby team)">Ospreys</a> 41–35 with tries from <a href="/wiki/Tom_Varndell" title="Tom Varndell">Tom Varndell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Croft" title="Tom Croft">Tom Croft</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ben_Kay" title="Ben Kay">Ben Kay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alesana_Tuilagi" title="Alesana Tuilagi">Alesana Tuilagi</a> to win the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Welsh_Cup" title="Anglo-Welsh Cup">EDF Energy Cup</a> at <a href="/wiki/Twickenham_Stadium" title="Twickenham Stadium">Twickenham Stadium</a>. This was quickly repeated with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guinness_Premiership" title="Guinness Premiership">Premiership</a> success on 12 May at Twickenham with a 44–16 win over <a href="/wiki/Gloucester_Rugby" title="Gloucester Rugby">Gloucester</a>. However Leicester failed to win an unprecedented treble, by losing the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heineken_Cup" title="Heineken Cup">Heineken Cup</a> Final at Twickenham on 20 May to <a href="/wiki/Wasps_RFC" title="Wasps RFC">Wasps</a>.</p>
<p>It was announced on 28 December 2006 that the head coach <a href="/wiki/Pat_Howard" title="Pat Howard">Pat Howard</a> would leave the club at the end of the season, to return to his native Australia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> He was succeeded by the then-head coach of <a href="/wiki/Argentina_national_rugby_union_team" title="Argentina national rugby union team">Argentina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marcelo_Loffreda" title="Marcelo Loffreda">Marcelo Loffreda</a> after the <a href="/wiki/2007_Rugby_World_Cup" title="2007 Rugby World Cup">2007 Rugby World Cup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> Loffreda guided Leicester through the group stages of the EDF cup to the semi final where they defeated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/London_Wasps" title="London Wasps">Wasps</a> in a knock-out game for the first time since the 1980s. This set up a rematch of the previous years final against the Ospreys, which Leicester lost. After losing all away games in the Heineken Cup that season Leicester failed to progress to the quarter finals. In the league Leicester struggled until a last minute last day try by <a href="/wiki/Tom_Varndell" title="Tom Varndell">Tom Varndell</a> beat <a href="/wiki/Harlequin_F.C." title="Harlequin F.C.">Harlequins</a> to set up a rematch of the previous seasons Premiership Final against Gloucester. Once again Leicester were successful late on, this time utilising <a href="/wiki/Andy_Goode" title="Andy Goode">Andy Goode</a>'s kicking to secure a last minute victory. In the final they had no such luck losing to perennial rivals Wasps. After this final; despite guiding Leicester to two Twickenham finals and only being in the job seven-months Loffreda was sacked.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cockerill_takes_the_reins">Cockerill takes the reins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leicester_Tigers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Cockerill takes the reins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Geordan_Murphy.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="499" height="289" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Geordan_Murphy.jpg/180px-Geordan_Murphy.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Geordan_Murphy.jpg/270px-Geordan_Murphy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Geordan_Murphy.jpg/360px-Geordan_Murphy.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Geordan_Murphy.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Geordan Murphy, pictured in 2012, played 322 games for Leicester between 1997 and 2013. He is the most decorated player in the club's history with 8 <a href="/wiki/English_Premiership_(rugby_union)" title="English Premiership (rugby union)">Premiership</a> titles, 2 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heineken_Cup" title="Heineken Cup">European titles</a> and 2 Anglo-Welsh cups.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Heyneke_Meyer" title="Heyneke Meyer">Heyneke Meyer</a> was the board's choice to replace Loffreda, however unfortunate family circumstances led to his resignation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Richard Cockerill took over until the end of the season, having guided Leicester to a home Heineken Cup quarter final against Bath. He was appointed head coach on 17 April 2009<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> and promoted to Director of Rugby on 19 July 2010<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> following Leicester's second Premiership title in as many years.</p>
<p>On Sunday 3 May 2009 Leicester Tigers made history in their <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_Blues_vs_Leicester_Tigers_(2008%E2%80%9309_Heineken_Cup)" title="Cardiff Blues vs Leicester Tigers (2008–09 Heineken Cup)">Heineken cup semi-final</a> against <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_Blues" title="Cardiff Blues">Cardiff</a> when for the first time in the competitions history a place kicking competition was required to decide the outcome. The teams were drawing 26–26 after normal time and there was no score during extra time. Leicester won this 7–6 after backrow forwards <a href="/wiki/Craig_Newby" title="Craig Newby">Newby</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jordan_Crane_(rugby_union)" title="Jordan Crane (rugby union)">Crane</a> both succeeded with their kicks at goal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2008-09_English_Premiership_(rugby_union)" title="2008-09 English Premiership (rugby union)">2009 Premiership final</a> Leicester beat London Irish (10–9), with a try from <a href="/wiki/Jordan_Crane_(rugby_union)" title="Jordan Crane (rugby union)">Crane</a> and 5 points from the boot of <a href="/wiki/Julien_Dupuy" title="Julien Dupuy">Dupuy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> The following week Leicester lost the <a href="/wiki/2009_Heineken_Cup_Final" title="2009 Heineken Cup Final">Heineken Cup final</a> in <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a> to Irish province <a href="/wiki/Leinster_Rugby" title="Leinster Rugby">Leinster</a>, containing former Leicester favourites captain <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leo_Cullen_(rugby_player)" title="Leo Cullen (rugby player)">Leo Cullen</a> and openside <a href="/wiki/Shane_Jennings" title="Shane Jennings">Shane Jennings</a>.</p>
<p>On Friday 6 November 2009 Leicester hosted the world champion <a href="/wiki/South_Africa_national_rugby_union_team" title="South Africa national rugby union team">Springboks</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> to mark the opening of the new stand on the north side of the ground. In a tight and compelling match a young Leicester side triumphed 22–17, with a try from <a href="/wiki/Lucas_Gonz%C3%A1lez_Amorosino" title="Lucas González Amorosino">Lucas González Amorosino</a> and 17 points from scrum half <a href="/wiki/Ben_Youngs" title="Ben Youngs">Ben Youngs</a>.</p>
<p>Tigers retained their Premiership title on 30 May 2010 as they defeated <a href="/wiki/Saracens_F.C." title="Saracens F.C.">Saracens</a> 33–27, coming back from behind 5 times in the match the win was secured by a crucial late try scored by <a href="/wiki/Dan_Hipkiss" title="Dan Hipkiss">Dan Hipkiss</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>Domestic success continued with Tigers reaching Premiership finals but losing in 2011 and 2012, against Saracens and Harlequins respectively. Silverware was still secured in 2012 though by winning the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2011-12_LV_Cup" title="2011-12 LV Cup">LV Cup</a> against Northampton at <a href="/wiki/Worcester_Warriors" title="Worcester Warriors">Worcester</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Sixways_Stadium" title="Sixways Stadium">Sixways Stadium</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> The competition was not viewed as highly as it was when Tigers won in 2007; it was primarily played on international game weekends and the final was no longer at Twickenham and held during the <a href="/wiki/Six_Nations_Championship" title="Six Nations Championship">Six Nations</a>.</p>
<p>In 2013 Tigers won their record extending 10th English title defeating local rivals <a href="/wiki/Northampton_Saints" title="Northampton Saints">Northampton Saints</a> 37–17 at <a href="/wiki/Twickenham_Stadium" title="Twickenham Stadium">Twickenham</a> despite losing fly half <a href="/wiki/Toby_Flood" title="Toby Flood">Toby Flood</a> to injury in the first half. Tries from <a href="/wiki/Niall_Morris" title="Niall Morris">Niall Morris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Graham_Kitchener" title="Graham Kitchener">Graham Kitchener</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manu_Tuilagi" title="Manu Tuilagi">Manu Tuilagi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vereniki_Goneva" title="Vereniki Goneva">Vereniki Goneva</a> sealed the match, with the final three tries coming after Northampton hooker Dylan Hartley's red card for verbally abusing referee Wayne Barnes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>Northampton gained their revenge the next year beating Tigers 21-20 in the Premiership semi final at Franklin's Gardens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> Tigers qualified for the play offs the next two years but suffered heavy away defeats to Bath (47-10)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> and Saracens (44-17).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>Leicester hold the record for most Premiership titles (10), the most consecutive Premiership Final appearances (9) and the most Play off appearances (12). They were the first team to achieve an away semi-final victory in the Premiership play-offs (against Gloucester at Kingsholm on 18 May 2008).</p>
<p>On Monday 2 January 2017, after a start to the season including a 34-21 defeat to Wasps at home,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> heavy defeats by Glasgow<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> and by Munster<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> in the European Champions Cup, Leicester's board decided to sack Richard Cockerill as director of rugby with immediate effect after a 16-12 home defeat by champions Saracens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Mauger" title="Aaron Mauger">Aaron Mauger</a> was placed in temporoary charge of the team whilst a full review of the club's coaching structure was undertaken.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
