<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name_and_colours">Name and colours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leicester_Tigers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Name and colours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nickname">Nickname</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leicester_Tigers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Nickname">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Martin_Johnson_and_Graham_Rowntree.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1440" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Martin_Johnson_and_Graham_Rowntree.jpg/230px-Martin_Johnson_and_Graham_Rowntree.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Martin_Johnson_and_Graham_Rowntree.jpg/345px-Martin_Johnson_and_Graham_Rowntree.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Martin_Johnson_and_Graham_Rowntree.jpg/460px-Martin_Johnson_and_Graham_Rowntree.jpg 2x" width="230"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Martin_Johnson_and_Graham_Rowntree.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Martin Johnson and Graham Rowntree in Tigers traditional colours during the friendly match vs. Bath in 2007.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The club's formal name is Leicester Football Club but is widely known by the nickname "Tigers". The first known use of the name was after a game against <a href="/wiki/Bedford_School" title="Bedford School">Bedford School</a> in February 1885, the <i>Leicester Daily Post</i> reporting that "the Tiger stripes were keeping well together".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> The origin of the nickname is uncertain most probably coming from the side's chocolate and yellow playing kit, but it may have come from the club's links to the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Leicestershire_Regiment" title="Royal Leicestershire Regiment">Leicestershire Regiment</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> who had received the nickname 'Tigers' after serving in <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">India</a>, and from 1825 had worn a cap-badge with a 'royal' tiger to mark the connection.</p>
<p>In their early years the side were also known as "The Death or Glory Boys" on account of their black shirts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colours">Colours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leicester_Tigers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Colours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Tigers' very first kit was black with white shorts and black socks, the shirt had the club's crest in the centre of the chest. From 1884 to 1887 the club played in chocolate and yellow shirts, likely giving rise to the club's nickname, white shorts and black socks before experimenting with claret and French grey horizontal stripes between 1887 and 1891.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first use of the iconic scarlet, green and white was on 3 October 1891 against <a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_RUFC" title="Milton Keynes RUFC">Wolverton</a> at Belgrave Cricket &amp; Cycle Ground. However, for the 1891/92 season the pattern was vertical stripes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> It was not until 1895 that the now traditional scarlet, green and white horizontal stripes were introduced to the jersey, paired with black shorts and socks until 1906.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> Tigers then played three season between 1906 and 1909 in white shirts with navy shorts, the first two season with a leaping Tiger logo on the left breast<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> before reverting to scarlet, green and white striped jersey but keeping the navy shorts. This new kit layout lasted until 1947 when the navy shorts were swapped for white.</p>
<p>Tigers kit and colours did not materially change between 1947 and 1999, only slight variations in the sizes of the stripes, the addition of a manufacturer's logo in 1975, a sponsor in 1988 and in 1991 the addition of the club crest for the first time since 1908.</p>
<p>In 1999 Tigers switched to a darker green and have played in a variety of kit designs since.</p>

<p>Tigers current kit was launched on 30 July 2016<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> and sees a return to the design worn between 1947 and 1999 as green, red and white stripes are pared with white shorts and black socks, with a green, red and white top. On 4 July 2016 it was announced that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holland_and_Barrett" title="Holland and Barrett">Holland and Barrett</a> would be the main shirt sponsors;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> other sponsors are Breedon Aggregates<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> who take a patch on the collarbone, Fischer Future Heat<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> who take a box above the players' number and <a href="/wiki/Stihl" title="Stihl">Stihl</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> who take a patch on the sleeve.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Premiership_play-offs">Premiership play-offs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leicester_Tigers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Premiership play-offs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Leicester_Tigers_v_Leinster_-_January_2008_(63)_H_Cup.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2136" data-file-width="2848" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Leicester_Tigers_v_Leinster_-_January_2008_%2863%29_H_Cup.jpg/220px-Leicester_Tigers_v_Leinster_-_January_2008_%2863%29_H_Cup.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Leicester_Tigers_v_Leinster_-_January_2008_%2863%29_H_Cup.jpg/330px-Leicester_Tigers_v_Leinster_-_January_2008_%2863%29_H_Cup.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Leicester_Tigers_v_Leinster_-_January_2008_%2863%29_H_Cup.jpg/440px-Leicester_Tigers_v_Leinster_-_January_2008_%2863%29_H_Cup.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Leicester_Tigers_v_Leinster_-_January_2008_(63)_H_Cup.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Leicester Tigers playing against Leinster in 2008.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Leicester have participated in the last 12 Premiership Play Offs, reaching nine consecutive finals between 2005 and 2013. The run ended when Leicester lost to a late <a href="/wiki/Northampton_Saints" title="Northampton Saints">Northampton</a> try in the 2014 semi finals.</p>
<p>Leicester finished first in the league table in 2004–05 going directly to the final; in <a href="/wiki/Martin_Johnson_(rugby_union)" title="Martin Johnson (rugby union)">Martin Johnson</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Neil_Back" title="Neil Back">Neil Back</a>'s last game for the club they lost 43–19 to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/London_Wasps" title="London Wasps">Wasps</a>. The following season Tigers finished second beating <a href="/wiki/London_Irish" title="London Irish">London Irish</a> 40–8 in their first ever Play Off semi final before once again losing the final, this time to <a href="/wiki/Sale_Sharks" title="Sale Sharks">Sale</a> who won 45–20 in wet conditions.</p>
<p>On 5 May 2007, Leicester defeated <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Rugby" title="Bristol Rugby">Bristol</a> 26–14 to reach the Premiership play-off final for the third consecutive year, where they defeated <a href="/wiki/Gloucester_Rugby" title="Gloucester Rugby">Gloucester</a> 44–16 at <a href="/wiki/Twickenham_Stadium" title="Twickenham Stadium">Twickenham</a> to win their first ever title via the playoffs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> On 18 May 2008 Leicester defeated Gloucester at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingsholm" title="Kingsholm">Kingsholm</a> to become the first team to win a Premiership semi-final playoff away from home. However this season also ended in defeat as Wasps won their sixth title, fourth via the play-offs.</p>
<p>In 2008–09 Tigers again topped the table and faced <a href="/wiki/Bath_Rugby" title="Bath Rugby">Bath</a> in the semi final winning 24–10. The final was the closest yet, Tigers defeated <a href="/wiki/London_Irish" title="London Irish">London Irish</a> by a single point thanks to <a href="/wiki/Jordan_Crane_(rugby_union)" title="Jordan Crane (rugby union)">Jordan Crane</a>'s try and five points from <a href="/wiki/Julien_Dupuy" title="Julien Dupuy">Julien Dupuy</a>. A year later <a href="/wiki/Richard_Cockerill" title="Richard Cockerill">Richard Cockerill</a>'s side retained the trophy with a 33–27 win against <a href="/wiki/Saracens_F.C." title="Saracens F.C.">Saracens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dan_Hipkiss" title="Dan Hipkiss">Dan Hipkiss</a> scored the decisive try in the closing stages.</p>
<p>Tigers reached the 2010–11 final for a rematch with Saracens which saw a record breaking seven minutes overtime played during which Leicester went through 32 phases camped on the Saracens try line before conceding a penalty which awarded Saracens their revenge for the previous years defeat.</p>
<p>2011–12 saw Tigers finish second in the table and face Saracens in the semi finals at Welford Road. Inspired by <a href="/wiki/George_Ford_(rugby_union)" title="George Ford (rugby union)">George Ford</a> and with tries from <a href="/wiki/Steve_Mafi" title="Steve Mafi">Steve Mafi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alesana_Tuilagi" title="Alesana Tuilagi">Alesana Tuilagi</a> Leicester were able to beat the Londoners 24–15 to meet <a href="/wiki/Harlequin_F.C." title="Harlequin F.C.">Harlequins</a> in the final. Ford was unable to reproduce his semi final form and <a href="/wiki/Nick_Evans_(rugby_union)" title="Nick Evans (rugby union)">Nick Evans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chris_Robshaw" title="Chris Robshaw">Chris Robshaw</a> inspired Quins to their maiden Premiership triumph.</p>
<p>Leicester finished 2nd in 2012–13 season playing Harlequins in a 33–16 win for the Tigers, to secure a place in the final and their ninth successive Premiership final, as well as this being their 13th Successive Semi-Final win in all competitions. Defeat of Northampton, 37–17, at the 2013 final means that Tigers achieved a record tenth Premiership title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<p>These nine consecutive finals is a record for consecutive appearances in a play-off final under the current format.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Stadium">Stadium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leicester_Tigers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Stadium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Welford_Road_Stadium" title="Welford Road Stadium">Welford Road Stadium</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:482px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Leicester_tigers_new_stand.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2310" data-file-width="3486" height="318" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Leicester_tigers_new_stand.jpg/480px-Leicester_tigers_new_stand.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Leicester_tigers_new_stand.jpg/720px-Leicester_tigers_new_stand.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Leicester_tigers_new_stand.jpg/960px-Leicester_tigers_new_stand.jpg 2x" width="480"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Leicester_tigers_new_stand.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The North stand</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The club plays its home games at <a href="/wiki/Welford_Road_Stadium" title="Welford Road Stadium">Welford Road Stadium</a>. The ground was opened in 1892 and the first stands accommodated 3,000 spectators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> The clubhouse was built on the Aylestone Road end in 1909,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> giving the curious situation of Welford Road Stadium's address being on the Aylestone Road. The Members' &amp; Crumbie Stands were built just before and just after the First World War respectively. A stand was built at the Welford Road end in 1995, initially called the Alliance &amp; Leicester Stand it is currently known as the <a href="/wiki/Mattioli_Woods" title="Mattioli Woods">Mattioli Woods</a> Stand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> The total ground capacity is currently 25,849 after the north stand (Members' Stand originally) was redeveloped in 2008 and Clubhouse stand in 2016, see below.</p>
<p>The newly opened clubhouse stand is a new all seating stand replacing the original clubhouse and an 1980s extension at the Aylestone Road end. Costing £6.7m the new stand has 2,917 spaces for general admittance &amp; 190 executive seats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> Replacing a temporary stand housing 992 places it has brought the capacity of the stadium to 26,000. The stand is currently known as the <a href="/wiki/Robin_Hood" title="Robin Hood">Robin Hood</a> Stand due to a sponsorship agreement with <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Building_Society" title="Nottingham Building Society">Nottingham Building Society</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<p>Before redevelopment of Welford Road began in 2008 the club explored many other options. On 23 November 2004 the club announced that it had entered into a 50–50 joint venture with the city's main <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_(soccer)" title="Football (soccer)">football</a> club, <a href="/wiki/Leicester_City_F.C." title="Leicester City F.C.">Leicester City</a>, to purchase City's current ground, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Walkers_Stadium" title="Walkers Stadium">Walkers Stadium</a>. If the purchase had gone through, the Tigers would have surrendered their lease on Welford Road and moved into Walkers Stadium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> However, after several months of talks, the two clubs could not agree as to which side would have priority at Walkers Stadium, and they ended any ground share plans in July 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 11 June 2007 the club announced plans that it was working with AFL, who were involved in redeveloping <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manchester_United" title="Manchester United">Manchester United</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Old_Trafford" title="Old Trafford">Old Trafford</a>, for a redevelopment plan which would raise the capacity from 17,498 to 25,000 by 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 20 February 2008 Leicester Tigers received planning consent for the £60million redevelopment of their Welford Road home.The first phase of the development would include space for 10,000 supporters in a new North Stand (Granby Halls side), taking capacity up from 17,498 to 24,000. After full renovation it will have a capacity of above 30,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the summer of 2008 work began on the construction of the new North Stand – then called the "Caterpillar Stand" after the club's main sponsor, <a href="/wiki/Caterpillar_Inc." title="Caterpillar Inc.">Caterpillar Inc.</a>, currently known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holland_and_Barrett" title="Holland and Barrett">Holland and Barrett</a> Stand again due to sponsorship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> The work was completed for the first home game of the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_English_Premiership_(rugby_union)" title="2009–10 English Premiership (rugby union)">2009-10 season</a> against <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_Falcons" title="Newcastle Falcons">Newcastle Falcons</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> The stand has room for 10,000 spectators along with a 1,000 seat hospitality suite. On the ground floor is the Final Whistle bar where no ticket is required for entry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the end of the 2008–09 season three home games were played at the <a href="/wiki/King_Power_Stadium" title="King Power Stadium">King Power Stadium</a>, then known as the Walkers Stadium, due to demolition of the old north stand. These saw Tigers play Bath twice, a dramatic 20-15 win in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heineken_Cup" title="Heineken Cup">Heineken Cup</a> quarter finals and a victory in the Premiership Play Off semi finals as well as a 73–3 demolition of <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Rugby" title="Bristol Rugby">Bristol</a>. Tigers have also played two Heineken Cup Semi Final games at the <a href="/wiki/King_Power_Stadium" title="King Power Stadium">King Power Stadium</a>, against <a href="/wiki/Stade_Toulousain" title="Stade Toulousain">Toulose</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scarlets" title="Scarlets">Llanelli Scarlets</a>, but the ground was designated as a neutral venue for both.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_squad">Current squad</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leicester_Tigers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Current squad">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">For player movements leading up to the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=2017%E2%80%9318_English_Premiership_(rugby_union)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="2017–18 English Premiership (rugby union) (page does not exist)">2017–18 season</a>, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_2017%E2%80%9318_Premiership_Rugby_transfers#Leicester_Tigers" title="List of 2017–18 Premiership Rugby transfers">List of 2017–18 Premiership Rugby transfers § Leicester Tigers</a>.</div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Internationals">Internationals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leicester_Tigers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Internationals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Leicester_Tigers_players_selected_for_International_rugby" title="List of Leicester Tigers players selected for International rugby">List of Leicester Tigers players selected for International rugby</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/List_of_Leicester_Tigers_players_selected_for_International_rugby" title="List of Leicester Tigers players selected for International rugby">136 players</a> from 13 different nations have been selected to represent their national side whilst a member of Leicester. The first was <a href="/wiki/Jack_Miles_(rugby_union)" title="Jack Miles (rugby union)">Jack Miles</a> who was selected for <a href="/wiki/England_national_rugby_union_team" title="England national rugby union team">England</a> in 1903, Leicester's first non-English international was <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_rugby_union_team" title="Scotland national rugby union team">Scotland's</a> <a href="/wiki/Jock_Lawrie" title="Jock Lawrie">Jock Lawrie</a> in 1924. The club's first non-British or Irish player selected for international duty was <a href="/wiki/Canada_national_rugby_union_team" title="Canada national rugby union team">Canada's</a> <a href="/wiki/Dave_Lougheed" title="Dave Lougheed">Dave Lougheed</a> when he played against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USA_national_rugby_union_team" title="USA national rugby union team">USA</a> in August 1998.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id=".C2.A0.C2.A0Lions_Tourists"><span style="padding-left:1px;"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Logo_Lions_Rugby.svg"><img alt="Logo Lions Rugby.svg" data-file-height="414" data-file-width="314" height="22" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/11/Logo_Lions_Rugby.svg/17px-Logo_Lions_Rugby.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/11/Logo_Lions_Rugby.svg/26px-Logo_Lions_Rugby.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/11/Logo_Lions_Rugby.svg/34px-Logo_Lions_Rugby.svg.png 2x" width="17"/></a><span style="padding-left:4px;"> </span>Lions Tourists</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leicester_Tigers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section:   Lions Tourists">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The following are players which have represented the <a href="/wiki/British_and_Irish_Lions" title="British and Irish Lions">Lions</a>, whilst playing for Leicester:</p>

<b><a href="/wiki/1983_British_Lions_tour_to_New_Zealand" title="1983 British Lions tour to New Zealand">1983</a>:</b> <a href="/wiki/Dusty_Hare" title="Dusty Hare">Dusty Hare</a><br/>
<b><a href="/wiki/1980_British_Lions_tour_to_South_Africa" title="1980 British Lions tour to South Africa">1980</a>:</b> <a href="/wiki/Paul_Dodge" title="Paul Dodge">Paul Dodge</a><br/>
<b><a href="/wiki/1974_British_Lions_tour_to_South_Africa" title="1974 British Lions tour to South Africa">1974</a>:</b> <a href="/wiki/Alan_Old" title="Alan Old">Alan Old</a><br/>
<b><a href="/wiki/1971_British_Lions_tour_to_New_Zealand" title="1971 British Lions tour to New Zealand">1971</a>:</b> <i><a href="/wiki/Rodger_Arneil" title="Rodger Arneil">Rodger Arneil</a></i><br/>
<b><a href="/wiki/1959_British_Lions_tour_to_Australia_and_New_Zealand" title="1959 British Lions tour to Australia and New Zealand">1959</a>:</b> <i><a href="/wiki/Tony_O%27Reilly" title="Tony O'Reilly">Tony O'Reilly</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Phil_Horrocks-Taylor" title="Phil Horrocks-Taylor">Phil Horrocks-Taylor</a><br/>
<b><a href="/wiki/1936_British_Lions_tour_to_Argentina" title="1936 British Lions tour to Argentina">1936</a>:</b> <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Gadney" title="Bernard Gadney">Bernard Gadney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Obolensky" title="Alexander Obolensky">Alexander Obolensky</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Beamish" title="Charles Beamish">Charles Beamish</a><br/>
<b><a href="/wiki/1930_British_Lions_tour_to_New_Zealand_and_Australia" title="1930 British Lions tour to New Zealand and Australia">1930</a>:</b> <a href="/wiki/Doug_Prentice" title="Doug Prentice">Doug Prentice</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Beamish" title="George Beamish">George Beamish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Kendrew" title="Douglas Kendrew">Joe Kendrew</a><br/>

<b><a href="/wiki/1908_British_Lions_tour_to_New_Zealand_and_Australia" title="1908 British Lions tour to New Zealand and Australia">1908</a>:</b> <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Stanley_Jackson" title="Frederick Stanley Jackson">F.S. Jackson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edward_Jackett" title="Edward Jackett">John Jackett</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_William_Smith" title="Thomas William Smith">Tom Smith</a><br/>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rugby_World_Cup">Rugby World Cup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leicester_Tigers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Rugby World Cup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wavell_Wakefield" title="Wavell Wakefield">Wavell Wakefield</a> <span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/England" title="England"><img alt="England" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="800" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/be/Flag_of_England.svg/23px-Flag_of_England.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/be/Flag_of_England.svg/35px-Flag_of_England.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/be/Flag_of_England.svg/46px-Flag_of_England.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> (1924, 4 tests)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Doug_Prentice" title="Doug Prentice">Doug Prentice</a> <span style="padding-left:1px;"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Logo_Lions_Rugby.svg"><img alt="Logo Lions Rugby.svg" data-file-height="414" data-file-width="314" height="22" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/11/Logo_Lions_Rugby.svg/17px-Logo_Lions_Rugby.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/11/Logo_Lions_Rugby.svg/26px-Logo_Lions_Rugby.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/11/Logo_Lions_Rugby.svg/34px-Logo_Lions_Rugby.svg.png 2x" width="17"/></a><span style="padding-left:4px;"> </span>(1930, 2 tests)</li>

<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/*" title="*">*</a> Martin Corry was also captain for the majority of a Lions test in 2005 after <a href="/wiki/Brian_O%27Driscoll" title="Brian O'Driscoll">Brian O'Driscoll</a> left the field injured, however he is not considered the official captain for that match.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Rugby_Hall_of_Fame">World Rugby Hall of Fame</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leicester_Tigers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: World Rugby Hall of Fame">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The following people associated with club have been inducted into the <a href="/wiki/World_Rugby_Hall_of_Fame" title="World Rugby Hall of Fame">World Rugby Hall of Fame</a>.</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-3" style="-moz-column-count: 3; -webkit-column-count: 3; column-count: 3;">
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tony_O%27Reilly" title="Tony O'Reilly">Tony O'Reilly</a> - Inducted in 2009<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Martin_Johnson_(rugby_union)" title="Martin Johnson (rugby union)">Martin Johnson</a> - Inducted in 2011<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Clive_Woodward" title="Clive Woodward">Clive Woodward</a> - Inducted in 2011<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bob_Dwyer" title="Bob Dwyer">Bob Dwyer</a> - Inducted in 2011<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Waisale_Serevi" title="Waisale Serevi">Waisale Serevi</a> - Inducted in 2013<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wavell_Wakefield,_1st_Baron_Wakefield_of_Kendal" title="Wavell Wakefield, 1st Baron Wakefield of Kendal">Wavell Wakefield</a> - Inducted in 2015<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Team_of_the_Century_and_Walk_of_Legends">Team of the Century and Walk of Legends</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leicester_Tigers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Team of the Century and Walk of Legends">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Tigers have named two "best" teams in recent times. On 1 November 2000 to celebrate the coming <a href="/wiki/Millennium" title="Millennium">millennium</a> a panel of former Tigers players and administrators named a <i>Team of the century</i>; whilst from October 2008 to February 2009 to celebrate the building of the then named <i>Caterpillar Stand</i> fans were invited to vote on a <i>Walk of Legends</i> in partnership with the <i><a href="/wiki/Leicester_Mercury" title="Leicester Mercury">Leicester Mercury</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
